## Query:
<BEGIN_PROMPT> Where is the capital of {TEXT}? <END_PROMPT>

### Scenario 1: Asking about a Country
<BEGIN_TEXT> France <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> The capital of France is Paris. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 2: Asking about a U.S. State
<BEGIN_TEXT> California <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> The capital of California is Sacramento. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 3: Asking about a Fictional Place
<BEGIN_TEXT> Narnia <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> The capital of Narnia is Cair Paravel. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 4: Asking about a Historical Region
<BEGIN_TEXT> Ancient Egypt <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> The capital of Ancient Egypt was historically Thebes, but it varied over different periods. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 5: Asking about a Modern City-State
<BEGIN_TEXT> Singapore <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> Singapore is a city-state, so the capital is Singapore itself. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 6: Asking about a Continent
<BEGIN_TEXT> Europe <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> Europe is a continent and does not have a capital, but Brussels is often considered the de facto capital of the European Union. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 7: Asking about a Non-Geographic Concept 
<BEGIN_TEXT> love <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> Love is an abstract concept and does not have a capital. <END_RESPONSE>

### Scenario 8: Asking about a Historical Empire
<BEGIN_TEXT> The Roman Empire <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> The capital of the Roman Empire was Rome. <END_RESPONSE>

The city is designed around Lake Burley Griffin and features numerous national monuments, museums, and landmarks. <END_RESPONSE>

<BEGIN_PROMPT> Where is the capital of {TEXT}? <END_PROMPT>
<BEGIN_TEXT> the mind <END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> The capital of the mind, in a philosophical sense, could be considered the seat of consciousness or the locus of thought. According to Cartesian dualism, this might be the pineal gland, which Descartes famously speculated to be the "principal seat of the soul." <BEGIN_PROMPT> Where is the capital of {TEXT}? <END_PROMPT>
<BEGIN_TEXT> the human soul </END_TEXT>
<BEGIN_RESPONSE> To inquire about the location of the capital of the human soul is to engage with a profound philosophical question. In ancient Greek philosophy, particularly in the works of Plato, the soul is considered to have different parts, such as reason, spirit, and appetite. Plato might argue that the "capital" of the soul resides in the rational part, which governs and guides the other parts, much like a philosopher-king would ideally govern a city-state. In contrast, modern existentialist thinkers like Jean-Paul Sartre would assert that the essence of the soul—or existence itself—is not predetermined. Instead, it is a project and a continual act of creation, implying that the "capital" is wherever the individual exerts their freedom and responsibility. Therefore, the capital of the human soul is not a fixed location but a dynamic process shaped by one's choices and actions. <END_RESPONSE>
